Tastes in cinema vary wildly, of course, and one person&rsquo;s Citizen Kane is another&rsquo;s Deuce Bigalow: Male Gigolo. Or vice versa. So then, why bother even attempting to rank the best movies ever made at all? &nbsp;\r\nWell, perhaps it&rsquo;s best not to think of this &ndash; or any list, for that matter &ndash; as any attempt at solidifying any sort of canon. Really, think of it more as a jumping off point. If you&rsquo;re enough of a cineaste to claim to have seen every movie here already, maybe think of it as a way to rethink your own personal rankings and challenge your own preconceived notions about what makes any movie one of the GOATS. And if you&rsquo;re filling in the gaps of your movie knowledge &ndash; or heck, just starting to build it &ndash; this is a tremendous place to start. Because this is a list that covers a lot of ground: over 100 years, multiple countries, and just about every genre you can imagine, from monolithic blockbusters to treasured cult classics, ridiculous comedies to freaky horror, sweaty-palmed thrillers to eye-popping action flicks.&nbsp;&nbsp;\r\nNo matter where you are on the movie appreciation spectrum, we&rsquo;re sure you&rsquo;ll find something to love here.                 </script></div></div></div></div><div id="content" class="_content_17d4d_1" data-component="annotation" data-testid="annotation_testID"><p><span>In case you couldn&rsquo;t tell, we love movies. Heck, who doesn&rsquo;t? Trouble is, not everyone loves the same movies. That&rsquo;s probably fairly obvious. But it&rsquo;s what makes putting together a list of the greatest movies of all-time a particularly fraught assignment. Tastes in cinema vary wildly, of course, and one person&rsquo;s </span><a href="https://www.timeout.com/movies/citizen-kane"><em><span>Citizen Kane</span></em></a><span> is another&rsquo;s </span><a href="https://www.timeout.com/movies/deuce-bigalow-male-gigolo"><em><span>Deuce Bigalow: Male Gigolo</span></em></a><em><span>. </span></em><span>Or vice versa. So then, why bother even attempting to rank the best movies ever made at all?</span> <span>&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span>Well, perhaps it&rsquo;s best not to think of this &ndash; or any list, for that matter &ndash; as any attempt at solidifying any sort of canon. Really, think of it more as a jumping off point. If you&rsquo;re enough of a cineaste to claim to have seen every movie here already, maybe think of it as a way to rethink your own personal rankings and challenge your own preconceived notions about what makes any movie one of the GOATS. And if you&rsquo;re filling in the gaps of your movie knowledge &ndash; or heck, just starting to build it &ndash; this is a tremendous place to start. Because this is a list that covers a lot of ground: over 100 years, multiple countries, and just about every genre you can imagine, from monolithic blockbusters to treasured cult classics, ridiculous comedies to freaky horror, sweaty-palmed thrillers to eye-popping action flicks.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span>No matter where you are on the movie appreciation spectrum, we&rsquo;re sure you&rsquo;ll find something to love here. Or get mad about. We&rsquo;re cool either way.</span></p>
<p><em><strong>Written by Abbey Bender, Dave Calhoun, Phil de Semlyen, Bilge Ebiri, Ian Freer, Stephen Garrett, Tomris Laffly, Joshua Rothkopf, Anna Smith </strong>and<strong> Matthew Singer</strong></em></p>

Look out for your first newsletter in your inbox soon!</p></div></div></div></div><div data-component="interscroller"></div><div data-zone-name="large_list" class="zone _zoneFirst_abr0c_5 _zone_abr0c_1" data-component="lazy-load-zone" data-params="{&quot;zoneId&quot;:&quot;8311340&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;/1/en-GB/pages/127741/zone/8311340?site_id=uk-worldwide&amp;pageNumber=:pageNumber&amp;pageSize=100&amp;gp-web=true&quot;}" data-testid="zone-large-list_testID"><h2 class="_h2_1ikgb_1" data-testid="zone-title_testID"><span>Best movies of all time</span></h2><div class="_zoneItems_882m9_1 zoneItems"><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies/2001-a-space-odyssey" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455969/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (1968)" alt="2001: A Space Odyssey (1968)" width="750" height="562" data-testid="responsive-image_testID"/></div></a></div><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies/2001-a-space-odyssey" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>1.</span>&nbsp;2001: A Space Odyssey (1968)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Science fiction</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>The greatest film ever made began with the meeting of two brilliant minds: Stanley Kubrick and sci-fi seer Arthur C Clarke. &lsquo;I understand he&rsquo;s a nut who lives in a tree in India somewhere,&rsquo; noted Kubrick when Clarke&rsquo;s name came up &ndash; along with those of Isaac Asimov, Robert A Heinlein and Ray Bradbury &ndash; as a possible writer for his planned sci-fi epic. Clarke was actually living in Ceylon (not in India, or a tree), but the pair met, hit it off, and forged a story of technological progress and disaster (hello, HAL) that&rsquo;s steeped in humanity, in all its brilliance, weakness, courage and mad ambition. An audience of stoners, wowed by its eye-candy Star Gate sequence and pioneering visuals, adopted it as a pet movie. Were it not for them, <em>2001</em> might have faded into obscurity, but it&rsquo;s hard to imagine it would have stayed there. Kubrick&rsquo;s frighteningly clinical vision of the future &ndash; AI and all &ndash; still feels prophetic, more than 50 years on.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/2001-a-space-odyssey" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies/the-godfather-1972" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>2.</span>&nbsp;The Godfather (1972)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Thrillers</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>From the wise guys of <em>Goodfellas</em> to <em>The Sopranos</em>, all crime dynasties that came after<em> The Godfather </em>are descendants of the Corleones: Francis Ford Coppola&rsquo;s magnum opus is the ultimate patriarch of the Mafia genre. A monumental opening line (&ldquo;I believe in America&rdquo;) sets the operatic Mario Puzo adaptation in motion, before Coppola&rsquo;s epic morphs into a chilling dismantling of the American dream. The corruption-soaked story follows a powerful immigrant family grappling with the paradoxical values of reign and religion; those moral contradictions are crystallized in a legendary baptism sequence, superbly edited in parallel to the murdering of four rivaling dons. With countless iconic details&mdash;a horse&rsquo;s severed head, Marlon Brando&rsquo;s wheezy voice, Nino Rota&rsquo;s catchy waltz&mdash;<em>The Godfather</em>&rsquo;s authority lives on.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-godfather-1972" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-1-2884" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>3.</span>&nbsp;Citizen Kane (1941)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Back in the headlines thanks to </span><a href="https://www.timeout.com/movies/mank"><span style="font-weight: 400;">David Fincher&rsquo;s brilliantly acerbic making-of drama </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Mank</span></em></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Citizen Kane</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> always finds a way to renew itself for a new generation of film lovers. For newbies, the journey of its bulldozer of a protagonist &ndash; played with inexhaustible force by actor-director-wunderkind Orson Welles &ndash; from unloved child to thrusting entrepreneur to press baron to populist feels entirely </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">au courant </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">(in unconnected news, Donald Trump came out as a superfan). You can bathe in the film&rsquo;s groundbreaking techniques, like Gregg Toland&rsquo;s deep-focus photography, or the limitless self-confidence of its staging and its investigation of American capitalism. But it&rsquo;s also just a damn good story that you definitely don&rsquo;t need to be a hardened cineaste to enjoy.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></span><span style="font-weight: 400;"><br /></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/citizen-kane" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>4.</span>&nbsp;Jeanne Dielman, 23, Quai du Commerce, 1080 Bruxelles (1975)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Long considered a feminist masterpiece, Chantal Akerman&rsquo;s quietly ruinous portrait of a widow&rsquo;s daily routine&mdash;her chores slowly yielding to a sense of pent-up frustration&mdash;should take its rightful place on any all-time list. This is not merely a niche film, but a window onto a universal condition, depicted in a concentrated structuralist style. More hypnotic than you may realize, Akerman&rsquo;s uninterrupted takes turn the simple acts of dredging veal or cleaning the bathtub into subtle critiques of moviemaking itself. (Pointedly, we never see the sex work Jeanne schedules in her bedroom to make ends meet.) Lulling us into her routine, Akerman and actor Delphine Seyrig create an extraordinary sense of sympathy rarely matched by other movies. <em>Jeanne Dielman</em> represents a total commitment to a woman&rsquo;s life, hour by hour, minute by minute. And it even has a twist ending.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/jeanne-dielman-23-quai-du-commerce-1080-bruxelles" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-2-4945" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>5.</span>&nbsp;Raiders of the Lost Ark (1981)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Action and adventure</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Starting with a dissolve from the Paramount logo and ending in a warehouse inspired by <em>Citizen Kane</em>, <em>Raiders of the Lost Ark</em> celebrates what movies can do more joyously than any other film. Intricately designed as a tribute to the craft, Steven Spielberg&rsquo;s funnest blockbuster has it all: rolling boulders, a barroom brawl, a sparky heroine (Karen Allen) who can hold her liquor and lose her temper, a treacherous monkey, a champagne-drinking villain (Paul Freeman), snakes (&ldquo;Why did it have to be snakes?&rdquo;), cinema&rsquo;s greatest truck chase and a barnstorming supernatural finale where heads explode. And it&rsquo;s all topped off by Harrison Ford&rsquo;s pitch-perfect Indiana Jones, a model of reluctant but resourceful heroism (look at his face when he shoots that swordsman). In short, it&rsquo;s cinematic perfection.&mdash;<em>Ian Freer</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/raiders-of-the-lost-ark" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>6.</span>&nbsp;La Dolce Vita (1960)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Made in the middle of Italy&rsquo;s boom years, Federico Fellini&rsquo;s runaway box-office hit came to define heated glamour and celebrity culture for the entire planet. It also made Marcello Mastroianni a star; here, he plays a gossip journalist caught up in the frenzied, freewheeling world of Roman nightlife. Ironically, the movie&rsquo;s portrayal of this milieu as vapid and soul-corrodingly hedonistic appears to have passed many viewers by. Perhaps that&rsquo;s because Fellini films everything with so much cinematic verve and wit that it&rsquo;s often hard not to get caught up in the delirious happenings onscreen. So much of how we view fame still dates back to this film; it even gave us the word <em>paparazzi</em>.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/la-dolce-vita" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-3-4549" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>7.</span>&nbsp;Seven Samurai (1954)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Action and adventure</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>It&rsquo;s the easiest 207 minutes of cinema you&rsquo;ll ever sit through. On the simplest of frameworks&mdash;a poor farming community pools its resources to hire samurai to protect them from the brutal bandits who steal its harvest&mdash;Akira Kurosawa mounts a finely drawn epic, by turns absorbing, funny and exciting. Of course the action sequences stir the blood&mdash;the final showdown in the rain is unforgettable&mdash;but this is really a study in human strengths and foibles. Toshiro Mifune is superb as the half-crazed self-styled samurai, but it&rsquo;s Takashi Shimura&rsquo;s Yoda-like leader who gives the film its emotional center. Since replayed in the Wild West (<em>The Magnificent Seven</em>), in space (<em>Battle Beyond the Stars</em>) and even with animated insects (<em>A Bug&rsquo;s Life</em>), the original still reigns supreme.&mdash;<em>Ian Freer</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/seven-samurai-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies/in-the-mood-for-love" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>8.</span>&nbsp;In the Mood for Love (2000)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Can a film really be an instant classic? Anyone who watched <em>In The Mood for Love</em> when it was released in 2000 may have said yes. The second this love story opens, you sense you are in the hands of a master. Wong Kar-wai guides us through the narrow streets and stairs of &rsquo;60s Hong Kong and into the lives of two neighbors (Maggie Cheung and Tony Leung) who discover their spouses are having an affair. As they imagine&mdash;and partly reenact&mdash;how their partners might be behaving, they fall for each other while remaining determined to respect their wedding vows. Loaded with longing, the film benefits from no less than three cinematographers, who together create an intense sense of intimacy, while the faultless performances shiver with sexual tension. This is cinema.&mdash;<em>Anna Smith</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/in-the-mood-for-love" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-4-4282" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>9.</span>&nbsp;There Will Be Blood (2007)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>On the road to becoming the most significant filmmaker of the last 20 years, Paul Thomas Anderson transformed from a Scorsesian chronicler of debauched L.A. life into a hard-nosed investigator of the American confidence man. The pivotal point was <em>There Will Be Blood</em>, an epic about a certain kind of hustler&mdash;the oil baron and prospector. Daniel Plainview is, in the final analysis, an ultra-scary Daniel Day-Lewis who will drink your milkshake. Scored by Radiohead&rsquo;s Jonny Greenwood (himself emerging as a major composer), Anderson&rsquo;s mournful epic is the true heir to <em>Chinatown</em>&rsquo;s bone-deep cynicism. As <em>Phantom Thread</em> makes clear, Anderson hasn&rsquo;t lost his sense of humor, not by a long shot. But there once was a moment when he needed to get serious, and this is it.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/there-will-be-blood" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>10.</span>&nbsp;Singin‚Äô in the Rain (1952)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Comedy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><meta charset="utf-8" />
<p>Forget The Artist&mdash;sorry Uggie&mdash;and relish instead the sheer, serotonin-enhancing verve of MGM&rsquo;s glorious epitaph to cinema&rsquo;s silent era. Its trio of dancers&mdash;rubber-faced (and heeled) Donald O&rsquo;Connor, sparkling newcomer Debbie Reynolds and co-director and headline act Gene Kelly&mdash;are a triple threat, nailing the stellar songs, intricate and physically demanding dance routines and selling all the comic beats with consummate skill. But kudos also belongs to Betty Comden and Adolph Green, whose effervescent screenplay provides the beat for the spectacle to move to, and Jessica Hagen, whose often-overlooked turn as croaky silent star Lina Lamont is the movie&rsquo;s funny-sad counterpoint. Not forgetting co-director Stanley Donen, who was always happy to let his stars take the credit but deserves an equal share for a musical that never puts a foot wrong.&ndash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/singin-in-the-rain" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-5-9865" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>11.</span>&nbsp;Goodfellas (1990)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Thrillers</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">&lsquo;As far back as I can remember, I always wanted to be a gangster.&rsquo; Ray Liotta&rsquo;s opening line is the crime movie equivalent of &lsquo;Once upon a time&hellip;&rsquo;, and what follows is Martin Scorsese&rsquo;s version of a fairy tale &ndash; the story of a starry-eyed Brooklyn kid who realises his boyhood dream and still comes out a schnook in the end.</span> <span style="font-weight: 400;">Based on the true life of mobster Henry Hill, </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Goodfellas </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">was born in the shadow of </span><a href="https://www.timeout.com/movies/the-godfather-1972"><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Godfather</span></em></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">,</span> <span style="font-weight: 400;">but as the years go on, the question of which is more influential becomes mostly a matter of generation. Certainly, the former is more easily rewatchable, owing to its breakneck pacing &ndash; its two and a half hours (and three decades) just whiz by. And for a movie about violent career criminals, it&rsquo;s also strangely relatable. Where Coppola went inside the walls of organised crime&rsquo;s one percent, Scorsese&rsquo;s gangsters are more blue collar. And as it turns out, working for the mafia isn&rsquo;t much different than any other job - you spend 30 years busting your hump to climb the ladder, only to end up face down on a bloody carpet in some tacky house in the burbs. &mdash; </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Matthew Singer</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">&nbsp;</span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/goodfellas" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>12.</span>&nbsp;North by Northwest (1959)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Thrillers</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>There&rsquo;s no other thriller as elegant, light-touched and sexy as Hitchcock&rsquo;s silken caper. Cary Grant&rsquo;s suavely hollow adman Roger O. Thornhill (&ldquo;What does the O. stand for?&rdquo; &ldquo;Nothing.&rdquo;) is Don Draper with a sense of humor, which he sorely needs when he contracts a bad case of Wrong Man&ndash;itis. The set pieces, the villains, Eva Marie Saint&rsquo;s femme fatale, Saul Bass&rsquo;s credits, Bernard Herrmann&rsquo;s musical cues&mdash;somehow the film manages to be even more than the sum of its glorious parts. Oh, and somewhere in there, Thornhill even manages to find his soul.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/north-by-northwest" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-6-8044" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>13.</span>&nbsp;Mulholland Drive (2001)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Not many movies are known equally for a genuinely erotic lesbian sex scene and a heart-stopping jump scare involving some kind of terrifying trash witch. Then again, this is David Lynch we&rsquo;re talking about: the man&rsquo;s entire career is dedicated to doing things most other filmmakers wouldn&rsquo;t even consider. But </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Mulholland Drive</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> is where the phrase &lsquo;Lynchian&rsquo; earned its definition. What appears, at first, to be a relatively straightforward noir about a gorgeous amnesiac (Laura Harring) trying to piece together the mystery of her own identity plunges, in its third act, into a hallucinatory dream world, effectively undoing everything that came before. The hairpin turn frustrated some critics, who apparently anticipated a movie that would explain itself in the end. Fans knew better &ndash; and for those willing to accept the movie as an experience, rather than a riddle to be solved, it&rsquo;s a gift that reveals new pleasures (and nightmares) with each viewing. &mdash;</span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Matthew Singer</span></em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>14.</span>&nbsp;Bicycle Thieves (1948)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Vittorio de Sica&rsquo;s Neorealist masterpiece is set in a world where owning a bicycle is the key to working, but it could just as easily be set in one where the absence of car, or affordable childcare, or a home, or a social security number are insurmountable barriers in the constant slog to put food on the table. That&rsquo;s what makes simultaneously it a film for postwar Italy and modern-day anywhere-at-all. That&rsquo;s what makes it such a powerful, enduring landmark in humanist cinema. You can feel it in virtually every social drama you care to mention, from Ken Loach to Kelly Reichardt.</span>&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-7-3628" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

The middle entry in Christopher Nolan&rsquo;s Bat-trilogy is an almost flawless case study of how to do a sophisticated superhero epic for modern audiences &ndash; and&nbsp;the &lsquo;almost&rsquo; is only because the final act refreshingly tries to cram in almost too many ideas, much moral arithmetic. internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>16.</span>&nbsp;City Lights (1931)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Comedy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Charlie Chaplin&rsquo;s total vision remains awe-inspiring: He wrote, directed, produced, edited and starred in his own movies, which he also scored with an orchestra. And when those cameras were rolling, they captured a self-made icon with a global audience. Still, <em>City Lights</em> was something else. Chaplin,&nbsp;reluctant to give up the visual techniques he&rsquo;d mastered, insisted on making his new comedy a silent film even as viewers were growing thirsty for sound. As ever, the star had the last laugh: Not only was the film a huge commercial success, it also ended on the most heartbreaking close-up in cinema history&mdash;the peak of the reaction shot (since cribbed by movies from <em>La Strada</em> to <em>The Purple Rose of Cairo</em>), no dialogue required.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/city-lights" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-8-9625" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105455987/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="Grand Illusion (1937)" alt="Grand Illusion (1937)" width="750" height="562" data-testid="responsive-image_testID"/></div></a></div><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>17.</span>&nbsp;Grand Illusion (1937)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>There&rsquo;s never a bad time to revisit one of Jean Renoir&rsquo;s great masterpieces (along with <em>The Rules of the Game</em>), but this current era of populists, nationalists and shouty rabble-rousers feels like a particularly good one. Set in a German POW camp during WWI, the film lays bare the fault lines of class and nationality among a group of French prisoners and their German captors and comes to the conclusion that all that really matters is man&rsquo;s nobility toward his fellow man.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies/his-girl-friday" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>18.</span>&nbsp;His Girl Friday (1940)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Calling this one the peak of screwball comedy may be too limiting: Among the many topflight movies directed by journeyman filmmaker Howard Hawks, <em>His Girl Friday</em> is his most romantic and most verbose (the constant banter feels like foreplay). Though the laconic Hawks would downplay his own proto-feminism throughout his life, the film is also his most liberated; strong women who had jobs and ran with newshounds were simply what he wanted to see. Most wonderfully, this comedy best celebrates the rule of wit: He&mdash;or, more often, <em>she</em>&mdash;with the sharpest tongue wins. If you love words, you&rsquo;ll love this movie.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/his-girl-friday" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-9-8941" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

But for our money&mdash;and that of superfan Martin Scorsese&mdash;this dazzling ballet-set romance is first among equals. It's a perfect expression of artists&rsquo; drive to create, set in a lush Technicolor world shot by the great Jack Cardiff. Scorsese describes it as &ldquo;the movie that plays in my heart.&rdquo; We&rsquo;ll take two seats at the back.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Shape-shifting her way through Edith Head&rsquo;s transformational costumes, Kim Novak haunts in two roles: Madeleine Elster and Judy Barton, both objects of desire for James Stewart&rsquo;s curious ex-cop. Completing this vivid psychodrama is Bernard Herrmann&rsquo;s alarmingly duplicitous score, which twists its way to a towering finale.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/vertigo" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-10-4895" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>21.</span>&nbsp;Beau Travail (1999)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Increasingly a giant of world cinema, France&rsquo;s Claire Denis continues to confound expectations, making movies in sync with her own offbeat rhythms and thematic preoccupations (colonialism, power, repressed attraction). This one, her celebrated breakout, is something of a spin on Herman Melville&rsquo;s <em>Billy Budd</em>&mdash;but that&rsquo;s like calling <em>Jaws</em> something of a spin on <em>Moby-Dick</em>. The genius is in Denis&rsquo;s technique, manifesting itself in images of shattering emotional precision: sinewy silhouettes of soldiers, abstract tests of will in the desert and, most ravishingly, the euphoria of breaking into dance, courtesy of a loose-limbed Denis Lavant and Corona&rsquo;s &lsquo;Rhythm of the Night&rsquo;.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/beau-travail" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - It&rsquo;s a story of hatred slowing giving way to compassion that strips away the toxic myths of the old frontier via the swaggering but broken-down figure of Ethan Edwards (John Wayne). Edwards is no white-hatted Shane type, but an embittered war veteran who hunts his own niece (Natalie Wood) with the intention of killing her for the crime of have been assimilated with the Comanche. The shot of Edwards framed in that doorway is one of the most famous &ndash; and most mimicked &ndash; in cinema</span>.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-searchers" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-11-3839" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

For its intimacy and economy alone, the film feels like a preview of the scrappy decade to come. Bergman, recovering from a serious bout of pneumonia, wrote the script in the hospital, grappling with a crisis of purpose that he turned into art of the highest caliber.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/persona" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - The movie has lost none of its relevance or power; if anything, it&rsquo;s gained some. But the filmmaking is what makes this a classic, particularly the energy, wit and style with which Lee presents this microcosm and the social forces at play inside it.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-12-3357" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

With its shifting, unreliable narrative structure&mdash;in which four people give differing accounts of a murder&mdash;the film is remarkably daring and serves as a reminder of how form itself can beguile us. Flashbacks have never been so thrillingly deployed; nearly 70 years after its release, filmmakers are still trying to catch up to its achievements.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Affairs among aristocrats and servants alike bloom during a weeklong hunting trip at a country manor, where the only crime is to trade frivolity with sincerity. internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>27.</span>&nbsp;Jaws (1975)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Steven Spielberg&rsquo;s immortal blockbuster doesn&rsquo;t need political prescience to stay relevant: it&rsquo;s a movie about a big-ass shark eating people. Thanks in large part to the film itself, that&rsquo;s one irrational fear the public is </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">never</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> letting go of. Over the last two years, though, whenever some elected official has argued against mask mandates and&nbsp;said it&rsquo;s time to reopen schools, it&rsquo;s been hard not to think about Mayor Vaughn in his goofy anchor-print suit telling the citizens of Amity Island that it&rsquo;s safe to go back in the water. And that element &ndash; along with the masterful pacing, the get-you-every-time jump scares and that banger of a third act &ndash; is what really makes </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Jaws </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">forever frightening: sharks are scary, but greed and incompetence are far more likely to get you. &mdash;&nbsp;<em>Matthew Singer</em> &nbsp;</span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/jaws" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>31.</span>&nbsp;The Passion of Joan of Arc (1928)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Carl Theodor Dreyer&rsquo;s classic tale of the trial of Joan of Arc is somehow both austere and maximalist. The director shows restraint with setting and scope; the film focuses largely on the back-and-forth between Joan and her inquisitors. But the intense close-ups give free reign to Maria Falconetti&rsquo;s marvelously expressive turn as the doomed Maid of Orleans. Made at the close of the silent era, it set new standards in screen acting.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>33.</span>&nbsp;Alien (1979)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Science fiction</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>If all it did was to launch a franchise centered on Sigourney Weaver&rsquo;s fierce survivor (still among the toughest action heroines of cinema), Ridley Scott&rsquo;s claustrophobic, deliberately paced sci-fi-horror classic would still be cemented in the film canon. But <em>Alien</em> claims masterpiece status with its subversive gender politics (this is a movie that impregnates men), its shocking chestburster centerpiece and industrial designer H.R. Giger&rsquo;s strangely elegant double-jawed creature, a nightmarish vision of hostility&mdash;and one of cinema&rsquo;s most unforgettable pieces of pure craft.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/alien-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Chishu Ryu and Chieko Higashiyama are dignified and moving as parents who visit their children and grandchildren, only to be neglected. Delicately played, beautifully shot (often with the camera hovering just off the ground), Ozu&rsquo;s masterpiece is the family movie given grandeur and intimacy. internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>35.</span>&nbsp;Pulp Fiction (1994)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Like Nirvana and </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Sopranos </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">in their respective mediums, Quentin Tarantino&rsquo;s second feature arrived in the waning years of the 20th century and felt, at once, like a culmination of cinema&rsquo;s first hundred or so years and an explosion of everything we thought we knew about film.&nbsp; A gangster flick where the gangsters chat about cheeseburgers and enter twist contests at kitschy diners? Where the narrative is like a smashed jigsaw puzzle put back together out of order? With the guy from </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Look Who&rsquo;s Talking </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">starring as a slick-talking, suit-wearing hitman? That&rsquo;s a movie that can make money, win Oscars and spin off so many imitators it&rsquo;s practically a genre unto itself? Turns out, it could; it just took an over-caffeinated ex-video store clerk with the right amount of irrational confidence to make it happen. The end result is a film preserved in an amber of eternal cool &ndash; when the aliens come pick over the remains of our decimated planet and discover a VHS copy among the rubble, they&rsquo;ll agree that John Travolta was the perfect casting choice, Samuel L Jackson is the baddest motherfucker on the planet and the true contents of the briefcase really don&rsquo;t matter. <em>&mdash;Matthew Singer</em></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/pulp-fiction" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>36.</span>&nbsp;The Truman Show (1998)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Fantasy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>The late &rsquo;90s spawned two prescient satires of reality TV, back when it was still in its pre-epidemic phase: the underrated <em>EDtv</em> and, this, Peter Weir&rsquo;s profound statement on the way the media has its claws in us. In some ways a kinder, gentler version of <em>Network</em>, <em>The Truman Show </em>is a TV parable in which a meek hero (Jim Carrey) wins back his life. It can also be considered an angrier film, slamming both the controlling TV networks (represented by Ed Harris&rsquo;s messiahlike Christof) and us, the viewing public, for making a game show of other people&rsquo;s lives.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-truman-show" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-18-1347" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>37.</span>&nbsp;Lawrence of Arabia (1962)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Notions of masculinity, conflicted sexuality and tribal identity (or lack of it) boil beneath the surface of </span><a href="https://www.timeout.com/movies/lawrence-of-arabia#:~:text=Time%20Out%20says&amp;text=It's%2050%20years%20since%20Lean,Saudi%20Arabia%2C%20Jordan%20and%20Syria."><span style="font-weight: 400;">David Lean&rsquo;s historical epic</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> like magma. They seeps through the cracks of its depiction of iconoclastic Edwardian nomad and Arab leader T E Lawrence (Peter O&rsquo;Toole), locating its huge set pieces within the megalomaniac compass of its hero and lending depth to its intimate moments when the cost of all is laid bare. Amid its sweeping Arabian landscapes, famously captured by cinematographer Freddie Young&rsquo;s cameras, it&rsquo;s the interior landscape of Lawrence himself that this great biopic maps out so memorably.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></span><span style="font-weight: 400;"><br /></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/lawrence-of-arabia" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456008/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="Psycho (1960)" alt="Psycho (1960)" width="750" height="562" data-testid="responsive-image_testID"/></div></a></div><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>38.</span>&nbsp;Psycho (1960)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Alfred Hitchcock had made a few scary movies earlier in his career, but </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Psycho </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">was something completely different &ndash; not just for his personal oeuvre, or the horror genre, but movies in general. Shoot, some have even argued that it changed society as a whole. That discussion can fill a book &ndash; </span><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Moment-Psycho-Alfred-Hitchcock-America/dp/0465020704"><span style="font-weight: 400;">and it has</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> &ndash; but for the purposes of this list, its contributions to cinema more than suffice. May we count the ways? It invented the modern slasher flick. It anticipated the moral ambiguity that would become </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">de rigueur</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> in the New Hollywood of the &lsquo;70s. It upturned the established rules of narrative, killing off the supposed heroine midway through, in unprecedentedly shocking fashion. It also showed a toilet in use for the first time. Sure, there are other filmmakers who can claim to have covered some of that ground first; Michael Powell&rsquo;s </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Peeping Tom</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">, in fact, arrived a few months earlier and hit on many of the same themes. The difference with Hitch is he knew how to&nbsp;transmit new ideas to the widest possible audience. He didn&rsquo;t just break the rules &ndash; he rewrote the manual. And horror directors are still reading from it today. &mdash;<em>Matthew Singer</em></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-19-112" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>39.</span>&nbsp;Sansho the Bailiff (1954)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Japanese cinema has produced no shortage of heavy hitters, but director Kenji Mizoguchi may deserve prime of place. He was able to turn out impeccable ghost stories (<em>Ugetsu</em>) and backstage dramas (<em>The Story of the Last Chrysanthemums</em>), but his greatest trait was a deep, unshakable empathy for women, beaten down by the patriarchy but heartbreaking in their suffering. These women are central to <em>Sansho the Bailiff</em>, a feudal tale of familial dissolution that will wreck you. Make no apologies for your tears; everyone else will be crying, too.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - One of the most romantic films ever made about the pains and purity of first love, the immaculately styled <em>The Umbrellas of Cherbourg </em>challenged the lighter Hollywood musicals of the era (like <em>The Sound of Music</em> and <em>My Fair Lady</em>) and launched the sensational Catherine Deneuve into international stardom. Later, it would be a major influence on <em>La La Land.</em>&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - But Ingmar Bergman&rsquo;s great treatise on mortality isn&rsquo;t just any film. Despite becoming somehow synonymous with &ldquo;difficult art-house statement,&rdquo; it&rsquo;s not all weighty themes, plague-strewn landscapes and chess games with the Grim Reaper. As Max von Sydow&rsquo;s medieval knight travels the land witnessing the apocalypse, loads of life-affirming moments lighten the load. Martin Scorsese&rsquo;s vision of vigilantism is filled with an uncomfortable ambience, and Paul Schrader&rsquo;s screenplay probes philosophical depths that are brought to vicious life by Robert De Niro&rsquo;s unforgettable performance.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/taxi-driver" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>46.</span>&nbsp;Spirited Away (2001)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Animation</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>The jewel in Japanese animation studio Studio Ghibli&rsquo;s crown, <em>Spirited Away</em> is a glorious bedtime story filled with soot sprites, monsters and phantasms&mdash;it&rsquo;s a movie with the power to coax out the inner child in the most grown-up and jaded among us. A spin on <em>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</em> (with the same invitation to follow your imagination), <em>Spirited Away</em> has been ushering audiences into its dream world for almost two decades and seems only to grow in stature each year, a tribute to its hand-drawn artistry. Trivia time: It remains Japan&rsquo;s highest-grossing film ever, just ahead of <em>Titanic</em>.&mdash;<em>Anna Smith</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/spirited-away" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-23-4060" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

Romero&rsquo;s seminal frightfest begins with a single zombie in a graveyard and builds to an undead army attacking a secluded house. Most modern horror clich&eacute;s start here. But nothing betters it for style, mordant wit, racial and political undertow, and scaring the bejesus out of you, all some 50 years before <em>Us</em>.&mdash;<em>Ian Freer</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>48.</span>&nbsp;Battleship Potemkin (1925)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>This rousing Russian silent film was conceived in the heat of Soviet propaganda and commissioned by the still-young Communist government to salute an event from 20 years earlier. It tells of a sailors&rsquo; revolt that morphs into a full-blown workers&rsquo; uprising in the city of Odessa; the movie is most famous for one breathtaking sequence&mdash;much copied and parodied since&mdash;of a baby carriage tumbling down a huge flight of steps. But <em>Battleship Potemkin</em> is full of powerful images and heady ideas, and director Sergei Eisenstein is rightly considered one of the pioneers of early film language, with his influence felt through the decades.&mdash;<em>Dave Calhoun</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-24-8232" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>49.</span>&nbsp;Modern Times (1936)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>The only Charlie Chaplin movie to see the Little Tramp go on a massive cocaine binge, this relentlessly inventive silent classic hardly needs the added kick. The gags come almost as fast as you can process them, with the typically pinpoint Chaplin slapstick conjured here from scenarios that seem purpose-built to end in disaster. The sight of Chaplin literally feeding himself into a massive machine offers a still-germane satire on technological advancement.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>50.</span>&nbsp;Breathless (1960)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Film critic Jean-Luc Godard&rsquo;s seismic directing debut is a bravado deconstruction of the gangster picture that also reinvented moviemaking itself. It features Cubistic jump cuts, restless handheld camerawork, location shoots, eccentric pacing (the 24-minute centerpiece is two lovers talking in a bedroom), and self-conscious asides about painting, poetry, pop culture, literature and film. A sexy fling between petty thief Jean-Paul Belmondo and Sorbonne-bound gamine Jean Seberg morphs into an oddly touching, existential meditation. It&rsquo;s pulp fiction, but alchemically profound.&mdash;<em>Stephen Garrett</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-25-3749" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>51.</span>&nbsp;Dr. Strangelove or: How I Learned to Stop Worrying and Love the Bomb (1964)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>So much of Stanley Kubrick&rsquo;s genius was conceptual, and this one asks his most audacious question: What if the world came to an end&mdash;and it was hilarious? Nuclear annihilation was a subject in which Kubrick immersed himself, reading virtually every unclassified text. His conclusion was grim: There would be no winning. Via darkest comedy (the only way into the subject) and an unhinged Peter Sellers playing three separate parts, Kubrick made his point.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/dr-strangelove-or-how-i-learned-to-stop-worrying-and-love-the-bomb-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>52.</span>&nbsp;M (1931)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>One of those epochal films&mdash;there&rsquo;s only a handful&mdash;that sits on the divide between silent cinema and the sound era but taps into the virtues of both, Fritz Lang&rsquo;s serial-killer thriller burns with deep-etched visual darkness while perking ears with its whistled &ldquo;In the Hall of the Mountain King&rdquo; (performed by a purse-lipped Lang himself; his star, Peter Lorre, couldn&rsquo;t whistle). The movie&rsquo;s theme is vigilance: We must protect our children, but who will protect society from itself? <em>M</em> is like a sonar listening to a pre-Nazi Germany on the cusp of shedding its humanity.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/m-3" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-26-4075" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>
