internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>53.</span>&nbsp;Blade Runner</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Science fiction</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Set in (eek!) 2019, Ridley Scott&rsquo;s vision of a dystopian future is one of the most stylish sci-fi films of all time. With a noir-inspired aesthetic and a haunting synth score by Vangelis (a massive influence on Prince), <em>Blade Runner</em> is iconic not just for its era-defining look, but also for its deeper philosophical examination of what it means to be human. Many have tried to imitate the film&rsquo;s uncanny vibe, but these rain-slicked streets and seedy vistas possess a singular menace.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/blade-runner-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - This film is arguably his sharpest and most psychologically complex; inarguably, it&rsquo;s his bitchiest. There is so much to love in Fassbinder&rsquo;s shag-carpeted showdown, which goes beyond the spectacle of two dueling fashionistas into a profound exploration of aging and obsolescence.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-bitter-tears-of-petra-von-kant" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-27-3175" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

Robert Rossellini was responsible for a few of them, including <em>Germany Year Zero</em> and this earlier drama of repression and resistance, which boasts not one but two of the most memorable death scenes in all of cinema.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/rome-open-city" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Max Schreck&rsquo;s insectlike performance as the bloodthirsty Count Orlok is just as transfixing and repulsive as it was almost a century ago. German Expressionist director F.W. Murnau&rsquo;s haunting images of a crepuscular world set the chilling standard for generations of cinematic nightmares.&mdash;<em>Stephen Garrett</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-28-8889" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

(1980)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Comedy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>With about 6,500 zingers to choose from, everyone has their favorite <em>Airplane!</em> gag. Directors David and Jerry Zucker and their partner in extreme silliness, Jim Abrahams, truly threw the kitchen sink at this dizzying spoof of the &rsquo;70s disaster movies that were all the rage at the time. Onscreen comedy, in turn, was modernized for what would be its most transforming decade. Our favorite joke? &ldquo;Looks like I picked the wrong week to quit amphetamines.&rdquo;&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/airplane" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Using her celebrity in a radical way, Scarlett Johansson is perfectly cast as an alien in human form who roams Glasgow trying to pick up men in her van. It was shot guerrilla-style on the streets of the Scottish city, so look out for the footage of genuinely baffled passersby.&mdash;<em>Anna Smith</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/under-the-skin-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-29-1922" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

This one is a nonstop barrage of chases, each more spectacularly elaborate and nightmarish than the last&mdash;but it&rsquo;s all combined with Miller&rsquo;s surreal, poetic sensibility, which sends it into the realm of art.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/mad-max-fury-road" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Anchored by Rodrigo Prieto&rsquo;s swoonworthy cinematography and a wistful Heath Ledger (whose performance toppled societal perceptions of masculinity), <em>Brokeback Mountain</em> is a milestone in LGBTQ art-house cinema. It reimagined the Western genre and became a part of the zeitgeist.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/brokeback-mountain" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>63.</span>&nbsp;The Blair Witch Project (1999)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Horror</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 1997, a group of no-name actors went into the Maryland backwoods with some handheld cameras, a loose script and a budget that wouldn&rsquo;t cover the catering on most of the other films on this list, and emerged with a blockbuster. Perhaps no movie in history has ever achieved more with less than Daniel Myrick and Eduardo S&aacute;nchez&rsquo;s atmospheric horror classic. For years, though, </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Blair Witch Project </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">was discussed as a triumph of marketing more than anything else. It was pushed by an ad campaign that played coy with the veracity of the allegedly &lsquo;found footage&rsquo;: did an amateur documentary crew </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">really </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">disappear in the woods while investigating a local myth? Sheer curiosity drove audiences to theatres en masse &ndash; and it wasn&rsquo;t uncommon to leave a screening and overhear confused grumbling in the lobby. Twenty-plus years and an oversaturation of lesser imitators later, it&rsquo;s easier to appreciate </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Blair Witch </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">as a master class of low-budget cinema. Honestly, if there&rsquo;s a scarier scene in the last two decades than when those children&rsquo;s hands imprint on the crew&rsquo;s tent in the middle of night, it surely cost a hell of a lot more to make.</span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-blair-witch-project" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies/all-the-presidents-men" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456036/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="All the President‚Äôs Men (1976)" alt="All the President‚Äôs Men (1976)" width="750" height="562" data-testid="responsive-image_testID"/></div></a></div><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies/all-the-presidents-men" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>64.</span>&nbsp;All the President‚Äôs Men (1976)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Many movies have been made depicting journalism as it happens. Vanishingly few get the process right, and even fewer manage to convey the obsessiveness, the anxious frustration and the exhilaration of chasing a big story. Alan J Pakula&rsquo;s movie about two reporters chasing </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">the</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> biggest story in American political history nails every beat. The achievement is especially remarkable considering that, at the time, the story could barely even be considered history: Nixon had resigned from office not even two years prior. But that nearness lends the film a living energy that would&rsquo;ve dulled with additional hindsight. Even with its unspoilable ending, Pakula and screenwriter William Goldman still managed to build an uncommonly nervy thriller that never digresses from the central narrative. No, you won&rsquo;t get much of an idea of who Woodward and Bernstein (played with typical &rsquo;70s naturalism by Dustin Hoffman and Robert Redford) are apart from their work. Instead, you just see the work &ndash; and in this case, that&rsquo;s more than enough.&nbsp;<em>&mdash;Matthew Singer</em></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/all-the-presidents-men" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-32-2675" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>65.</span>&nbsp;The Apu trilogy (1955, 1956, 1959)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>We&rsquo;re cheating by including all three films (<em>Pather Panchali</em>, <em>Aparajito</em> and <em>The World of Apu</em>), but really, how do you separate the installments of Satyajit Ray&rsquo;s magnificent coming-of-age trilogy? The Bengali great follows young Apu (Apurba Kumar Roy) from boyhood to adult life via schooling and a move from his remote village to the big city, as well as loves and losses. Some of the most intimate Indian cinema ever captured, it&rsquo;s also completely relatable, whether you hail from Kolkata, Kansas or Camden Town.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>66.</span>&nbsp;The General (1926)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Comedy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Boy meets train. Boy loses train. Boy chases Union forces who stole train, wins back train and fires off in the opposite direction. It may not sound like your average love story, but that&rsquo;s exactly what Buster Keaton&rsquo;s deadpan and death-defying silent comedy is: a majestic demonstration of trick photography, balletic courage and comic timing, all underpinned by genuine heart. Trust us, it&rsquo;s loco-motional.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-general-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-33-2546" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

The sci-fi&ndash;inflected tale of two halves of a broken-up couple going through a memory-erasing procedure takes many surprising, poignant turns; the film&rsquo;s impeccably executed combination of authentically quirky imagery and philosophical inquiry has become a signpost of modern independent cinema.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/eternal-sunshine-of-the-spotless-mind" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - That&rsquo;s not to say Tobe Hooper&rsquo;s masterpiece doesn&rsquo;t deliver. internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>69.</span>&nbsp;Come and See (1985)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">As unsparing as cinema gets, the influence of Elem Klimov&rsquo;s sui generis war movie transcends the genre in a way that not even Steven Spielberg&rsquo;s <em>Saving Private Ryan</em> can match. At its heart it&rsquo;s a coming-of-age story that follows a young Belarusian boy (Aleksei Kravchenko) through unspeakable horror as Nazi death squads visit an apocalypse on his region. Alongside its historical truths, the film&rsquo;s grammar and visual language&mdash;there are passages that play like an ultra-violent acid trip&mdash;are what truly elevates it. Like an Hieronymus Bosch masterpiece, the images here can never be unseen.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/come-and-see" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - In weaving their stories together, Mann presents dueling but equally weighted perspectives, with our allegiance as viewers constantly shifting. Still, it&rsquo;s shocking to remember that<em> The Shining</em>&mdash;so redolent of the director&rsquo;s pet themes of mazelike obsession and the banality of evil&mdash;was once considered a minor work. It&rsquo;s since come to represent the most concentrated blast of Kubrick&rsquo;s total command; he&rsquo;s the god of the film, Steadicam-ing around corners and making the audience notice that he was born to redefine horror. A landmark of independent black cinema, it&rsquo;s set to a great soundtrack ranging from blues and classical to Paul Robeson. Poetic, compassionate, angry, ironic: All human life is present here.&mdash;<em>Ian Freer</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/killer-of-sheep" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - But respect must be paid to the performer, too: In a decade of brilliant acting, no turn was quite as galvanizing as the one given by Gena Rowlands in this stunning peek into a fraying mind. A fluky Los Angeles housewife and mother who&rsquo;s constantly being told to calm down, Rowlands&rsquo;s Mabel is the apotheosis of John Cassavetes&rsquo;s improvisatory cinema; our concern for her never flags as she teeters through excruciating scenes of breakdown and regrouping.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/a-woman-under-the-influence-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-37-1317" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

Fritz Lang&rsquo;s silent vision of a totalitarian society still astounds through its stunning cityscapes, groundbreaking special effects and a bewitchingly evil robot (Brigitte Helm). It&rsquo;s science fiction at its most ambitious and breathtaking&mdash;the not-so-modest beginnings of onscreen genre seriousness.&mdash;<em>Ian Freer</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/metropolis-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - (There&rsquo;s not a band out there without at least one Spinal Tap moment to its name.) Christopher Guest, Michael McKean and Harry Shearer are comic royalty, and we can only genuflect in their presence; shortly after this film, Guest kicked off his own directorial brand of humor, directly inspired by Rob Reiner&rsquo;s heavy-metal satire.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/this-is-spinal-tap" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Frank Capra&rsquo;s hilarious hate-at-first-sight love story is still one of the fastest movies ever made. Claudette Colbert&rsquo;s spoiled heiress and Clark Gable&rsquo;s opportunistic reporter hit the road and bicker their way toward a happily-ever-after ending, class barriers be damned. Not only did this smart and suggestively sexy pre-Code screwball shape every rom-com that followed, it still has a leg up on most of them.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-40-261" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>81.</span>&nbsp;Die Hard (1988)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Action and adventure</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Let&rsquo;s get this out of the way: </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Die Hard</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> is a Christmas movie. Deal with it. Another, less controversial statement about John McTiernan&rsquo;s blockbuster: it&rsquo;s the platonic ideal of an action movie, and Bruce Willis as wiseass New York cop John McClane is the coolest action hero of all-time. The sequels would stretch the limits of his charisma by getting bigger and stupider, but the original hits the perfect amount of big and brash, as McClane attempts to thwart the plans of a European terrorist group that&rsquo;s seized an LA high-rise and taken his wife hostage. But the truest reason </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Die Hard </span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;">succeeds to the degree it does &ndash; aside from the cracking dialogue, spectacular stunts and small details, i.e. McClane being forced to fight a bunch of terrorists in his bare foot &ndash; is that McClane has the ideal foil in Alan Rickman&rsquo;s Hans Gruber, who might also be the best action movie villain of all-time, an erudite pseudo-revolutionary who makes it clear that he reads </span><em><span style="font-weight: 400;">Forbes</span></em><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and doesn&rsquo;t much care for garrulous American cowboys.</span></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/die-hard" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - Part psychoanalysis session, part colorful genre fantasia, director Bernardo Bertolucci&rsquo;s enormously influential drama journeys through different styles and aesthetics. As much as Orson Welles&rsquo;s <em>Citizen Kane</em> did with the films of the &rsquo;20s, &rsquo;30s, and early &rsquo;40s, <em>The Conformist </em>offers a powerful compendium of cinematic techniques from the eras preceding it.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-41-9120" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>83.</span>&nbsp;The Thing (1982)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Let John Carpenter&rsquo;s real masterpiece&mdash;the one that horror mavens bow down to&mdash;take its place in the pantheon. A passion project that got clobbered by audiences and critics alike, <em>The Thing</em> was, in fact, that rarest of remakes: one that improves upon its source. Carpenter&rsquo;s widescreen elegance and spooky synth minimalism (here furthered by composer Ennio Morricone) found a new counterpoint in some of the most disgusting practical special effects ever sprung on a paying audience. But the film&rsquo;s ice-cold paranoia, uncut and pharma-grade, has been its most lasting legacy: a template of perfection for all since.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>84.</span>&nbsp;Daughters of the Dust (1991)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Writer-director Julie Dash should have become an Ava DuVernay-level success after her poetic feature debut, an achievement of otherworldly beauty. The first film made by an African-American woman to receive theatrical distribution, <em>Daughters of the Dust</em> is permeated with pride, history and matriarchal wisdom. Set in 1902, it follows the Gullah, descendents of slaves living off the coast of South Carolina, who painfully reckon with their fading traditions. Singularly ahead of its time, <em>Daughters</em> mourns the enduring tragedy of enslavement. Its tranquil strength later found an echo in Beyonc&eacute;&rsquo;s <em>Lemonade</em>.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-42-9659" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>85.</span>&nbsp;Barry Lyndon (1975)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Back in 1975, Stanley Kubrick&rsquo;s somber adaptation of William Makepeace Thackeray&rsquo;s novel about a young Irishman&rsquo;s journey from lovestruck exile to cynical grifter in 18th-century Europe seemed out of step with the gritty, intense output of contemporary cinema. Years later, it&rsquo;s considered by many to be Kubrick&rsquo;s masterpiece, and its deliberate, highly aestheticized approach has influenced everybody from Ridley Scott to Yorgos Lanthimos.&mdash;<em>Bilge Ebiri</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/barry-lyndon" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456064/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="Raging Bull (1980)" alt="Raging Bull (1980)" width="750" height="562" data-testid="responsive-image_testID"/></div></a></div><div class="articleContent _articleContent_kc5qn_216"><div class="_title_kc5qn_9 _titleNoCredit_kc5qn_197"><a href="/movies" class="" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>86.</span>&nbsp;Raging Bull (1980)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Martin Scorsese&rsquo;s hallucinogenic biography of the tenacious boxer Jake LaMotta (Robert De Niro) is a bold mash-up of neorealist grit and hyperstylized, gossamer beauty. Put on the gloves and LaMotta is in his element; take them off and he&rsquo;s an insecure sociopath consumed by sexual jealousy. De Niro&rsquo;s monstrous portrayal is miraculously empathetic, but what&rsquo;s truly revolutionary is Scorsese&rsquo;s technique: Like a modern-day Verdi, the Italian-American auteur elevates the profane to the operatic.&mdash;<em>Stephen Garrett</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-43-1986" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>87.</span>&nbsp;Seven (1995)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>David Fincher is the most signature director of his era: a crafter of iconic music videos and decade-defining dramas like <em>Zodiac</em> and<em> The Social Network</em>. But his transition to Hollywood was rocky; it was a town that barely understood him. The turning point was <em>Seven</em>, the first time that Fincher&rsquo;s fearsome vision arrived uncut. Stylistically, the dark movie (shot by an inspired Darius Khondji, working with a silver-nitrate-retention process) has proven more durable than even <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>, but it&rsquo;s that meme-able sucker punch of an ending that still rattles audiences.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - It&rsquo;s colder, greedier here: Klaus Kinski&rsquo;s conquistador craves gold, not culture. Featuring a river journey, a haunting, synthy Popul Voh score and a bunch of taunting monkeys, it&rsquo;s Herzog&rsquo;s <em>Apocalypse Now</em>.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/aguirre-wrath-of-god" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-44-6566" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>89.</span>&nbsp;The Battle of Algiers (1966)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Political thrillers still owe a debt to Gillo Pontecorvo&rsquo;s ever-timely tour de force. Recounting the Algerian uprising against French colonial occupiers in the 1950s, <em>The Battle of Algiers</em> boldly examines terrorism, racism and even torture as a means of intelligence-gathering. Screened at the Pentagon for its topical significance during the early phases of the Iraq War, <em>Algiers</em> has its rebellious legacy vested in numerous politically charged epics, from <em>Z</em> to Steven Spielberg&rsquo;s <em>Munich</em>.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-battle-of-algiers-1" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>90.</span>&nbsp;Women on the Verge of a Nervous Breakdown (1988)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Comedy</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Pedro Almod&oacute;var broke into the mainstream with this gloriously colorful ensemble comedy, an entry point for many into a style of smart, sexually liberated European cinema. <em>Women on the Verge of a Nervous Breakdown</em> offers juicy roles for a range of Spain&rsquo;s finest female actors (plus a charmingly baby-faced Antonio Banderas) and consistently delights with its creative choices in costuming and interior design. The combination of screwball dynamics and the garishness of the 1980s is perfectly calibrated and fun.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/women-on-the-verge-of-a-nervous-breakdown" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-45-7114" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

Still, <em>Boyhood</em>&rsquo;s astonishing compactness catches you off guard like no other movie. Adorned by Linklater&rsquo;s signature effortless rhythms, the film bottles the fleeting spirit of time, maturing into a reflective meditation on life&rsquo;s ordinary moments.&mdash;<em>Tomris Laffly</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/boyhood" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>92.</span>&nbsp;The Discreet Charm of the Bourgeoisie (1972)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Movies have always been a gateway into radical art; Hollywood may have made them sleek and accessible, but experimentation was there from the start. Luis Bu&ntilde;uel counts among the top rank of dreamers to ever grace the field of filmmaking. Without him, there&rsquo;s no David Lynch, no Wong Kar-wai&mdash;even Alfred Hitchcock was a fan. Of Bu&ntilde;uel&rsquo;s many seismic features (don&rsquo;t skip his slicin&rsquo;-up-eyeballs short, &ldquo;Un Chien Andalou&rdquo;), begin with this radical satire of class warfare, which sums up everything he did well. It even won him an unlikely Oscar.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/the-discreet-charm-of-the-bourgeoisie" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-46-4897" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>93.</span>&nbsp;Paths of Glory (1957)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>An antiwar movie, a courtroom thriller, an upstairs-downstairs study of social status, a religious critique, an absurdist satire and, finally, a heartbreakingly futile plea for compassion in the face of destruction, Stanley Kubrick&rsquo;s humanist masterpiece dissects all the delusional facets of the male psyche. Battlegrounds abound&mdash;psychological, emotional, physical&mdash;making the bleakly entrenched soldiers of 1916, and the officers who confuse folly for fame, still feel painfully relevant.&mdash;<em>Stephen Garrett</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><article class="tile _article_kc5qn_1" data-testid="tile-zone-large-list_testID"><div class="_imageContainer_kc5qn_33"><a href="/movies" class="tileImageLink" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;in content&quot;,&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><div class="_imageWrap_kc5qn_229"><img src="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/750/562/image.jpg" srcSet="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==" data-srcset="https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/380/285/image.jpg 380w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/750/562/image.jpg 750w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/1024/768/image.jpg 1024w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/1372/1029/image.jpg 1372w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/1536/1152/image.jpg 1536w,https://media.timeout.com/images/105456072/1920/1440/image.jpg 1920w" data-sizes="auto" class="lazyload _image_kc5qn_33 aspect-ratio-4-3" title="Secrets &amp; It can often be months before the camera rolls. The results have been consistently exquisite over the years, funneled into period musical-comedies (<em>Topsy-Turvy</em>) and brutal contemporary dramas (<em>Naked</em>) alike. We recommend Leigh&rsquo;s critical breakthrough, featuring nervy turns by Brenda Blethyn and Timothy Spall, as the perfect place to begin your deep dive.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-47-1061" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

It&rsquo;s a seedy, intoxicating tale that unfolds in Manhattan&rsquo;s backroom bar booths, and it features brain-searing performances from Tony Curtis as Sidney Falco, a bottom-feeding gossip monger, and Burt Lancaster as J.J. Hunsecker, a towering, corrupt newspaper columnist. The dialogue is snappy and delicious; the morals are as empty as Times Square at dawn&mdash;<em>Dave Calhoun</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/sweet-smell-of-success" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>97.</span>&nbsp;Nashville (1975)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>This multilayered epic of country music, politics and relationships is Robert Altman&rsquo;s signature achievement. With its overlapping dialogue and roving camera, <em>Nashville</em> created an earthy, idiosyncratic panorama of American life, featuring many of the most memorable actors of the decade. The 1970s were U.S. cinema&rsquo;s most exciting period, and <em>Nashville</em>&mdash;broadened by its admirable scope and freewheeling energy&mdash;is emblematic of that creativity.&mdash;<em>Abbey Bender</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/nashville" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>98.</span>&nbsp;Don‚Äôt Look Now (1973)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Drama</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Nicolas Roeg influenced and inspired a generation of filmmakers, from Danny Boyle to Steven Soderbergh&nbsp;&ndash; and here&rsquo;s why. Roeg shrouds Daphne du Maurier&rsquo;s short story in an icy chill, seeding the idea of supernatural forces at play in a wintry Venice through sheer filmmaking craft and the power of his editing. He finds a deep humanity in the horror, too, with Julie Christie and Donald Sutherland&rsquo;s grieving parents reconnecting and drifting apart like flotsam on some invisible tide. His masterpiece, <em>Don&rsquo;t Look Now</em> remains&nbsp;a primal cry of grief that shakes you to&nbsp;the core.&mdash;<em>Phil de Semlyen</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/dont-look-now" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;,&quot;category&quot;:&quot;GP Engagement&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:&quot;read more button&quot;}}" data-testID="view-more-cta_testID"><span class="_textContent_12eii_36">Read more</span></a></div></div></div></article><div class="_adsInline_882m9_6"><div data-testid="inline-generated-ad_testID" class="_inlineAdWrapper_1elek_65"><div class="_inlineAdContainer_1elek_60"><span class="caps xs-block xs-text-10 xs-mb2 xs-text-center _inlineAdHeader_1elek_75">Advertising</span><div class="_inlineAd_1elek_60"><div id="ad-list-49-7799" class="_ad_1elek_1 _ad-list_1elek_54 " data-testid="ad_testID"><script>

internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>99.</span>&nbsp;Bonnie and Clyde (1967)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Thrillers</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Arthur Penn&rsquo;s game-changing action film was made in the same spirit of the revisionist Westerns of the &rsquo;60s and &rsquo;70s&mdash;irreverent, fun, morally all over the place, and unafraid of blood and bullets. The movie takes us back to the 1930s during the legendary crime spree of lovers Bonnie Parker (Faye Dunaway) and Clyde Barrow (Warren Beatty), careening around Depression-era America and robbing it blind. Why did this film resonate so well at the end of its decade? With the Vietnam War, inner-city rioting and Nixon on the rise, all bets were off. Add the swoony pair of Beatty and Dunaway, and you&rsquo;ve got a classic on your hands: a revolution in period dress.&mdash;<em>Dave Calhoun</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/bonnie-and-clyde" target="_self" rel="" data-data-layer="{&quot;triggerOn&quot;:0,&quot;payload&quot;:{&quot;action&quot;:&quot;link - internal&quot;}}" data-testid="tile-link_testID"><h3 class="_h3_cuogz_1" data-testid="tile-title_testID"><span>100.</span>&nbsp;Get Out (2017)</h3></a></div><div class="_tileTags_kc5qn_44"><section class="_tags_163gl_1" data-testid="tags_testID"><ul class="_tagsList_163gl_5"><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Film</span></li><li class="_tag_163gl_1"><span class="_text_163gl_28">Horror</span></li></ul></section></div><div class="_summary_kc5qn_21"><p>Watch this space: Jordan Peele&rsquo;s newly minted horror classic is sure to rise in the rankings. Taking cues from grand master George A. Romero and his counterculture-defining <em>Night of the Living Dead</em>, Peele infused white liberal guilt with a scary racial subtext; the &ldquo;sunken place&rdquo; is precisely the kind of metaphor that only horror movies can exploit to the fullest. During its theatrical run&mdash;which stretched into a summer that also saw the white-supremacist Charlottesville rally&mdash;<em>Get Out</em> felt like the only movie speaking to a deepening divide.&mdash;<em>Joshua Rothkopf</em></p></div><div class="_ctaButtons_kc5qn_43"><div class="_cta_kc5qn_43 _viewMoreCta_kc5qn_105"><a class="_a_12eii_1" href="/movies/get-out" target="_self" rel=""
